10, 22]]}, "abstract": "<jats:sec>\n<jats:title />\n<jats:p>The smallest unit of life is a cell, which contains numerous protein molecules. Most\nof the functions critical to the cell\u2019s survival are performed by these proteins located in its different\norganelles, usually called \u2018\u2018subcellular locations\u201d. Information of subcellular localization\nfor a protein can provide useful clues about its function. To reveal the intricate pathways at the\ncellular level, knowledge of the subcellular localization of proteins in a cell is prerequisite.\nTherefore, one of the fundamental goals in molecular cell biology and proteomics is to determine\nthe subcellular locations of proteins in an entire cell. It is also indispensable for prioritizing\nand selecting the right targets for drug development. Unfortunately, it is both timeconsuming\nand costly to determine the subcellular locations of proteins purely based on experiments.\nWith the avalanche of protein sequences generated in the post-genomic age, it is highly\ndesired to develop computational methods for rapidly and effectively identifying the subcellular\nlocations of uncharacterized proteins based on their sequences information alone. Actually,\nconsiderable progresses have been achieved in this regard. This review is focused on those\nmethods, which have the capacity to deal with multi-label proteins that may simultaneously\nexist in two or more subcellular location sites. Protein molecules with this kind of characteristic\nare vitally important for finding multi-target drugs, a current hot trend in drug development.\nFocused in this review are also those methods that have use-friendly web-servers established so\nthat the majority of experimental scientists can use them to get the desired results without the\nneed to go through the detailed mathematics involved.</jats:p>\n</jats:sec>", "DOI": "10.2174/0929867326666190507082559", "type": "journal-article", "created": {"date-parts": [[2019, 5, 7]], "date-time": "2019-05-07T08:25:58Z", "timestamp": 1557217558000}, "page": "4918-4943", "update-policy": "http://dx.doi.org/10.2174/bsp_crossmark_policy", "source": "Crossref", "is-referenced-by-count": 12, "title": ["Advances in Predicting Subcellular Localization of Multi-label Proteins and its Implication for Developing Multi-target Drugs"], "prefix": "10.2174", "volume": "26", "author": [{"given": "Kuo-Chen", "family": "Chou", "sequence": "first", "affiliation": [{"name": "Gordon Life Science Institute, Boston, MA 02478, United States"}]}], "member": "965", "reference": [{"key": "ref=1", "doi-asserted-by": "publisher", "first-page": "1", "DOI": "10.1016/j.ab.2007.07.006", "volume": "370", "author": "Chou K.C.", "year": "2007", "unstructured": "Chou K.C.; Shen H.B.; Recent progress in protein subcellular location prediction. "abstract": "<jats:sec>\n<jats:title />\n<jats:p>&lt;P&gt;Background/Objective: Information of protein subcellular localization is crucially important\nfor both basic research and drug development. With the explosive growth of protein sequences\ndiscovered in the post-genomic age, it is highly demanded to develop powerful bioinformatics\ntools for timely and effectively identifying their subcellular localization purely based on the\nsequence information alone. Recently, a predictor called \u201cpLoc-mEuk\u201d was developed for identifying\nthe subcellular localization of eukaryotic proteins. Its performance is overwhelmingly better\nthan that of the other predictors for the same purpose, particularly in dealing with multi-label systems\nwhere many proteins, called \u201cmultiplex proteins\u201d, may simultaneously occur in two or more\nsubcellular locations. Although it is indeed a very powerful predictor, more efforts are definitely\nneeded to further improve it. This is because pLoc-mEuk was trained by an extremely skewed dataset\nwhere some subset was about 200 times the size of the other subsets. Accordingly, it cannot\navoid the biased consequence caused by such an uneven training dataset.\n&lt;/P&gt;&lt;P&gt;\nMethods: To alleviate such bias, we have developed a new predictor called pLoc_bal-mEuk by\nquasi-balancing the training dataset. Cross-validation tests on exactly the same experimentconfirmed\ndataset have indicated that the proposed new predictor is remarkably superior to pLocmEuk,\nthe existing state-of-the-art predictor in identifying the subcellular localization of eukaryotic\nproteins. It has not escaped our notice that the quasi-balancing treatment can also be used to deal\nwith many other biological systems.\n&lt;/P&gt;&lt;P&gt;\nResults: To maximize the convenience for most experimental scientists, a user-friendly web-server\nfor the new predictor has been established at http://www.jci-bioinfo.cn/pLoc_bal-mEuk/.\n&lt;/P&gt;&lt;P&gt;\nConclusion: It is anticipated that the pLoc_bal-Euk predictor holds very high potential to become\na useful high throughput tool in identifying the subcellular localization of eukaryotic proteins, particularly\nfor finding multi-target drugs that is currently a very hot trend trend in drug development.&lt;/P&gt;</jats:p>\n</jats:sec>", "DOI": "10.2174/1573406415666181218102517", "type": "journal-article", "created": {"date-parts": [[2018, 12, 20]], "date-time": "2018-12-20T10:34:38Z", "timestamp": 1545302078000}, "page": "472-485", "update-policy": "http://dx.doi.org/10.2174/bsp_crossmark_policy", "source": "Crossref", "is-referenced-by-count": 11, "title": ["pLoc_bal-mEuk: Predict Subcellular Localization of Eukaryotic Proteins by General PseAAC and Quasi-balancing Training Dataset"], "prefix": "10.2174", "volume": "15", "author": [{"given": "Kuo-Chen", "family": "Chou", "sequence": "first", "affiliation": [{"name": "Gordon Life Science Institute, Boston, MA 02478, United States"}]}, {"given": "Xiang", "family": "Cheng", "sequence": "additional", "affiliation": [{"name": "Gordon Life Science Institute, Boston, MA 02478, United States"}]}, {"given": "Xuan", "family": "Xiao", "sequence": "additional", "affiliation": [{"name": "Gordon Life Science Institute, Boston, MA 02478, United States"}]}], "member": "965", "reference": [{"key": "ref=1", "doi-asserted-by": "crossref", "first-page": "259", "DOI": "10.1016/S1534-5807(02)00216-2", "volume": "3", "author": "Ehrlich J.S.", "year": "2002", "unstructured": "Ehrlich JS, Hansen MD, Nelson WJ.
